2:21:1055:0:14:72:370:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Positive Long Run Capital Taxation: Chamley-Judd Revisited
2:22:1113:14:14:72:233:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Ludwig Straub and Iván Werning
2:23:1143:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 20441
2:24:1171:14:14:72:134:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:August 2014
2:25:1182:14:28:72:153:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. H2,H63
2:26:1196:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:F:ABSTRACT
2:27:1204:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:According to the Chamley-Judd result, capital should not be taxed in the long run. In this paper, we
2:28:1304:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:overturn this conclusion, showing that it does not follow from the very models used to derive them.
2:29:1403:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:For the model in Judd (1985), we prove that the long run tax on capital is positive and significant,
2:30:1503:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:whenever the intertemporal elasticity of substitution is below one. For higher elasticities, the tax converges
2:31:1613:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:to zero but may do so at a slow rate, after centuries of high capital taxation. The model in Chamley
2:32:1713:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:(1986) imposes an upper bound on capital taxation and we prove that the tax rate may end up at this
2:33:1812:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:bound indefinitely. When, instead, the bounds do not bind forever, the long run tax is indeed zero;
2:34:1911:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:however, when preferences are recursive but non-additive across time, the zero-capital-tax limit comes
2:35:2013:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:accompanied by zero private wealth (zero tax base) or by zero labor taxes (first best). Finally, we explain
2:36:2120:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:why the equivalence of a positive capital tax with ever rising consumption taxes does not provide a
2:37:2219:14:42:72:254:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:firm rationale against capital taxation.
2:38:2259:42:14:72:144:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:Ludwig Straub
2:39:2272:14:14:72:226:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics, MIT
2:40:2300:14:14:72:197:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:77 Massachusetts Avenue
2:41:2323:14:14:72:184:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:Cambridge, MA 02139
2:42:2342:14:28:72:149:350:12:Times:12:Times:F:straub@mit.edu
2:43:2356:28:14:72:138:322:12:Times:12:Times:F:Iván Werning
2:44:2368:14:14:72:245:308:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics, E17-234
2:45:2400:14:14:72:94:294:12:Times:12:Times:F:MIT
2:46:2403:14:14:72:197:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:77 Massachusetts Avenue
2:47:2426:14:14:72:184:266:12:Times:12:Times:F:Cambridge, MA 02139
2:48:2445:14:14:72:124:252:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER

3:50:2469:0:31:136:475:653:427:g_d0_f1:427:g_d0_f1:C:Positive Long Run Capital Taxation:
3:51:2504:31:0:189:421:622:427:g_d0_f1:427:g_d0_f1:C:Chamley-Judd Revisited
3:52:2526:0:47:422:429:629:223:g_d0_f2:223:g_d0_f2:C:∗
3:53:2527:47:23:189:287:582:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:Ludwig Straub
3:54:2540:23:0:225:252:559:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:MIT
3:55:2543:0:23:333:422:582:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:Iván Werning
3:56:2555:23:29:364:391:559:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:MIT
3:57:2558:29:62:266:345:530:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:August 2014
3:58:2569:62:17:101:510:468:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:According to the Chamley-Judd result, capital should not be taxed in the long run. In
3:59:2654:17:16:101:510:451:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:this paper, we overturn this conclusion, showing that it does not follow from the very
3:60:2740:16:17:101:510:435:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:models used to derive them. For the model in Judd (1985), we prove that the long
3:61:2820:17:17:101:510:418:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:run tax on capital is positive and significant, whenever the intertemporal elasticity of
3:62:2908:17:17:101:510:401:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:substitution is below one. For higher elasticities, the tax converges to zero but may
3:63:2993:17:17:101:510:384:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:do so at a slow rate, after centuries of high capital taxation. The model in Chamley
3:64:3077:17:17:101:510:367:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:(1986) imposes an upper bound on capital taxation and we prove that the tax rate may
3:65:3161:17:16:101:510:350:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:end up at this bound indefinitely. When, instead, the bounds do not bind forever, the
3:66:3246:16:17:101:510:334:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:long run tax is indeed zero; however, when preferences are recursive but non-additive
3:67:3331:17:17:101:510:317:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:across time, the zero-capital-tax limit comes accompanied by zero private wealth (zero
3:68:3417:17:17:101:510:300:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:tax base) or by zero labor taxes (first best). Finally, we explain why the equivalence
3:69:3503:17:17:101:510:283:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:of a positive capital tax with ever rising consumption taxes does not provide a firm
3:70:3587:17:46:101:261:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:F:rationale against capital taxation.
3:71:3622:46:31:72:197:220:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:1  Introduction
3:72:3637:31:18:72:540:189:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:One of the most startling results in optimal tax theory is the famous finding byJudd
3:73:3721:18:18:72:540:171:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(1985) andChamley(1986).  Although working independently, in somewhat different
3:74:3800:18:18:72:540:153:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:settings and, thus, complementing each other, their conclusions were strikingly similar:
3:75:3888:18:18:72:540:135:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:capital should go untaxed in any steady state. This implication, dubbed the Chamley-
3:76:3972:18:18:72:540:117:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Judd result, is commonly interpreted as applying in the long run, since convergence to a
3:77:4060:18:16:85:539:99:62:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f3:F:∗This paper benefited from detailed comments by Fernando Alvarez, Peter Diamond, Mike Golosov and
3:78:4157:16:11:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:Stefanie Stantcheva and was very fortunate to count with research assistance from Greg Howard, Lucas
3:79:4257:11:0:72:298:72:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:Manuelli and Andrés Sarto. All errors are our own.
4:80:4308:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:steady state is quite naturally taken for granted.1The takeaway is that taxes on capital
4:81:4396:18:18:72:253:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:should be zero, at least eventually.
4:82:4432:18:18:89:539:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Economic reasoning sometimes holds its surprises. The Chamley-Judd result is not
4:83:4512:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:at all obvious and was not anticipated by economists’ intuition, despite a large body of
4:84:4600:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:work at the time on the incidence of capital taxation and on optimal tax theory more
4:85:4684:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:generally. It represented a major watershed from a theoretical standpoint. One may even
4:86:4771:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:say that the result is downright puzzling, as witnessed by the fact that economists have
4:87:4859:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:since then taken turns putting forth differing intuitions to interpret it, none definitive nor
4:88:4953:18:18:72:223:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:universally accepted to date.
4:89:4982:18:18:89:539:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Theoretical wonder aside, a crucial issue is the result’s applicability. Many have ques-
4:90:5070:18:18:72:539:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tioned the model’s assumptions, especially that of infinitely-lived agents (e.g.Banks and
4:91:5159:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Diamond,2010). Still others have set up alternative models, searching for different con-
4:92:5247:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:clusions. These efforts notwithstanding, opponents and proponents alike acknowledge
4:93:5330:18:17:72:522:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Chamley-Judd as one of the most important benchmarks in the optimal tax literature.
4:94:5413:17:18:89:539:457:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Here we question the Chamley-Judd results directly, on their own ground and argue
4:95:5494:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that, even within the logic of these models, a zero long-run tax result does not follow.
4:96:5582:18:18:72:539:421:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:For both the models inJudd(1985) andChamley(1986), we provide results showing
4:97:5659:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:a positive long-run tax when the intertemporal elasticity of substitution is less than or
4:98:5748:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:equal to one. We conclude that these models do not actually provide a coherent argument
4:99:5835:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:against capital taxation, quite the contrary. We briefly discuss what went wrong with the
4:100:5924:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:original results, their interpretations and proofs—which are deceivingly straightforward,
4:101:6013:18:18:72:429:331:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:but, unfortunately, are just as deceiving as they are straightforward.
4:102:6083:18:18:89:539:313:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Before summarizing our results in greater detail, it is useful to briefly recall the se-
4:103:6171:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tups inJudd(1985) andChamley(1986). Start with the similarities. Both papers studied
4:104:6255:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:infinitely-lived agents. The models take as given an initial stock of capital and restrict
4:105:6345:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tax instruments to proportional taxes on capital and labor. Lump-sum taxes are limited
4:106:6431:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:or excluded, as are capital levies or other forms of capital expropriation. The tax rate is
4:107:6522:17:18:72:245:224:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:constrained by an upper bound.2
4:108:6553:18:20:89:539:206:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Turning to differences,Chamley(1986) focused on a representative agent and assumed
4:109:6635:20:15:85:540:186:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:1To quote from a few examples,Judd(2002): “[...] settingτkequal to zero in the long run [...] vari-
4:110:6734:15:12:72:540:171:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:ous results arguing for zero long-run taxation of capital; see Judd (1985, 1999) for formal statements and
4:111:6840:12:12:72:539:159:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:analyses.”Atkeson et al.(1999): “By formally describing and extending Chamley’s (1986) result [...] This
4:112:6944:12:12:72:540:147:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:approach has produced a substantive lesson for policymakers: In the long run, in a broad class of envi-
4:113:7047:12:12:72:539:135:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:ronments, the optimal tax on capital income is zero.”Phelan and Stacchetti(2001): “A celebrated result of
4:114:7152:12:12:72:540:123:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:Chamley (1986) and Judd (1985) states that with full commitment, the optimal capital tax rate converges
4:115:7255:12:12:72:539:111:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:to zero in the steady state.”Saez(2013): “The influential studies by Chamley (1986) and Judd (1985) show
4:116:7359:12:9:72:384:99:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:that, in the long-run, optimal linear capital income tax should be zero.”
4:117:7432:9:16:85:540:90:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:2Neither consumption taxes that mimic the effects of an initial wealth expropriation (Coleman II,2000),
4:118:7535:16:0:72:486:74:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:nor dividend taxes with capital expenditure (investment) deductions (Abel,2007) are allowed.
5:119:7628:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:perfect financial markets, with unconstrained government debt.Judd(1985) emphasizes
5:120:7711:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneity and redistribution in a two-class economy, with workers and capitalists.
5:121:7797:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:In addition, the model features financial market imperfections: workers do not save and
5:122:7884:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the government balances its budget, i.e. debt is restricted to zero.3As discussed inJudd
5:123:7972:18:18:72:539:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(1985), it is most remarkable that a zero long-run tax result obtains despite the restriction
5:124:8065:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:to budget balance.4Although extreme, imperfections of this kind may capture relevant
5:125:8149:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:aspects of reality, such as the limited participation in financial markets, the skewed distri-
5:126:8243:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:butions of wealth and the problems one that may accompany high levels of government
5:127:8326:18:18:72:181:564:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:debt or asset levels..5
5:128:8349:18:18:89:540:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We begin with the model inJudd(1985). We show that taxes may remain positive
5:129:8425:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:even in the long run. When the intertemporal elasticity of substitution (IES) is below
5:130:8511:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:one, taxes rise and converge towards a positive limit tax, instead of declining towards
5:131:8598:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:zero. This limit tax is significant and drives capital to its lowest feasible level. Indeed,
5:132:8690:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:as government spending falls, the lowest feasible capital stock approaches zero, and, the
5:133:8779:17:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:limit tax rate goes to infinity. The long run tax is not zero, far from it: it is large and
5:134:8870:18:18:72:197:439:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:potentially unbounded.
5:135:8892:18:18:89:539:421:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:When the IES is above one, we verify numerically that the solution converges to the
5:136:8975:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:zero-tax steady state. However, we show that this convergence may be very slow, some-
5:137:9060:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:times taking centuries for wealth taxes to drop below 1%. Indeed, in the neighborhood of
5:138:9148:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:a unitary IES, the speed of convergence is not bounded away from zero. Thus, even when
5:139:9234:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the long-run tax on capital is zero, this property provides a misleading summary of the
5:140:9321:18:18:72:206:331:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:model’s full implications.
5:141:9347:18:18:89:540:313:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We then turn to the representative agent Ramsey model studied byChamley(1986).
5:142:9425:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:As is well appreciated, in this setting, upper bounds on the taxation of capital are imposed
5:143:9517:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:in order to avoid the trivial solution involving expropriatory levels of initial taxation of
5:144:9609:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:capital. We provide two sets of results. First, we show that if the bounds on capital
5:145:9694:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:taxation are not binding in the long run, then the tax is indeed zero. However, we show
5:146:9781:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that for recursive nonadditive utility, this zero tax limit is necessarily accompanied by
5:147:9870:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:either zero private wealth converging to zero—in which case the tax base is zero—or the
5:148:9957:18:20:72:540:188:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:labor tax converging to zero—in which case the first best is achieved. This suggests that
5:149:10046:20:15:85:539:168:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:3Chamley(1986) offered a few extensions to heterogeneous agents andJudd(1985) also considered an-
5:150:10143:15:9:72:381:153:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:other model where workers, just as capitalists, can also save in capital.
5:151:10216:9:16:85:539:144:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:4Because of the presence of financial restrictions and imperfections,Judd(1985) model does not fit the
5:152:10318:16:12:72:539:128:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:standard Arrow-Debreu framework, nor the optimal tax theory developed around it such asDiamond and
5:153:10416:12:8:72:140:116:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:Mirrlees(1971).
5:154:10431:8:16:85:539:108:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:5Without constraints on debt, capitalists may become highly indebted or not own the capital they man-
5:155:10532:16:12:72:540:92:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:age. This idea that investment requires “skin in the game” is popular in the finance literature and macroeco-
5:156:10641:12:0:72:539:80:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:nomic models with financial frictions (seeBrunnermeier et al.,2012;Gertler and Kiyotaki,2010, for surveys).
6:157:10749:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:zero taxes are only attained after high taxation that either obliterates private wealth or
6:158:10839:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:allows the government to proceed without any distortionary taxation. Needless to say,
6:159:10924:18:18:72:477:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:these are not the scenarios envisioned by proponents of zero capital taxation.
6:160:11002:18:18:89:539:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Second, we show that the upper bounds imposed on the tax rate may bind forever,
6:161:11081:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:when the intertemporal elasticity of substitution is below one, implying a positive long-
6:162:11170:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:run tax on capital. We prove that this is guaranteed whenever debt is high enough. Im-
6:163:11256:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:portantly, the debt level required is below the peak of the Laffer curve, so this result is not
6:164:11351:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:driven by budgetary necessity. Intuitively, elevated levels of debt ensure high labor taxes,
6:165:11443:18:18:72:486:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:making capital taxation relatively attractive, helping to ease a high tax burden.
6:166:11524:18:18:89:540:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:In a setting very close to that ofChamley(1986),Judd(1999) presents an argument
6:167:11603:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:against positive capital taxation without requiring convergence to a steady state. How-
6:168:11690:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ever, we show that these arguments fail, because they involve assumptions on endoge-
6:169:11774:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:nous multipliers that are actually violated at the optimum.  We also explain why the
6:170:11858:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:observation discussed in that paper that capital taxation amounts to ever increasing con-
6:171:11947:17:18:72:489:457:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:sumption taxes, does not provide a rationale against indefinite capital taxation.
6:172:12028:18:18:89:539:439:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:To conclude, we present a hybrid model that combines heterogeneity and redistribu-
6:173:12110:18:18:72:539:421:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tion, as inJudd(1985), but allowing for government debt, as inChamley(1986). Capital
6:174:12194:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:taxation is especially potent in this setting. When upper bounds are imposed, the opti-
6:175:12281:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:mum indefinite taxation at the bound. This suggests that positive long run taxation may
6:176:12368:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:be expected in a wide range of models that are descendants ofChamley(1986) andJudd
6:177:12450:18:47:72:106:349:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(1985).

10:301:17919:18:18:72:539:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:vanish in equation (2d). Thus, the two situations that prevent the theorem’s application
10:302:18007:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:are: (i) non-convergence to an interior steady state; or (ii) non-convergence of multipliers.
10:303:18100:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:In general, one expects that (i) implies (ii). The literature has provided an example of (ii)
10:304:18193:18:28:72:398:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:where the allocation does converge to an interior steady state.
10:305:18256:28:18:72:539:536:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Theorem 2.(Lansing,1999;Reinhorn,2002 and 2013)Suppose the allocation converges to an
10:306:18341:18:18:72:540:518:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:interior steady state, so that ct,Ct,kt+1converge to positive values. Then, if and only ifσ=1,
10:307:18435:18:27:72:225:500:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:multipliers do not converge and
10:308:18466:27:17:239:250:473:143:g_d0_f5:80:g_d0_f5:C:R∗t
10:309:18469:17:0:240:251:456:143:g_d0_f5:80:g_d0_f5:C:Rt
10:310:18471:0:0:257:269:464:155:g_d0_f2:155:g_d0_f2:C:→

10:313:18474:0:36:283:374:464:155:g_d0_f7:143:g_d0_f3:A:(1−γ(1−β)υ∗),
10:314:18487:36:18:72:540:428:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:whereυ∗=limυt. This implies a positive long-run tax on capital if redistribution towards
10:315:18575:18:27:72:232:410:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:workers is desirable,1−γυ>0.
10:316:18603:27:18:89:540:383:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The result follows easily by combining (2c) and (2d) for the case withσ=1 and
10:317:18680:18:18:72:539:365:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:comparing it to the capitalist’s Euler equation, which requiresRt=1βat a steady state.
10:318:18766:18:18:72:540:347:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Lansing(1999) first presented the logarithmic case as a counterexample toJudd(1985).
10:319:18850:18:18:72:540:329:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Reinhorn(2002 and 2013) correctly clarified that in the logarithmic case the Lagrange
10:320:18935:18:18:72:370:311:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:multipliers explode, explaining the difference in results.8
10:321:18994:18:18:89:539:293:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Lansing(1999) depicts the result forσ=1 as a knife-edged case: “the standard
10:322:19070:18:18:72:540:275:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:approach to solving the dynamic optimal tax problem yields the wrong answer in this
10:323:19153:18:18:72:540:257:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(knife-edge) case [...]” (from the Abstract, page 423) and “The counterexample turns out
10:324:19241:18:18:72:540:239:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:to be a knife-edge result. Any small change in the capitalists’ intertemporal elasticity of
10:325:19332:18:18:72:540:221:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:substitution away from one (the log case) will create anticipation effects [...] As capitalists’
10:326:19428:18:18:72:540:203:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:intertemporal elasticity of substitution in consumption crosses one, the trajectory of the
10:327:19518:18:18:72:540:185:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:optimal capital tax in this model undergoes an abrupt change.” (page 427) This suggests
10:328:19605:18:19:72:531:167:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that forσ�=1 the long-run tax on capital is zero. We shall show that this is not the case.
10:329:19695:19:15:85:539:148:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:8Instead,Lansing(1999) suggests there may be a technical problem with the argument inJudd(1985)
10:330:19790:15:12:72:539:133:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:specific toσ=1. We see no technical difficulty in applying optimal control to the logarithmic case. We
10:331:19892:12:0:72:383:121:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:believe the issue is exactly whatReinhorn(2002 and 2013) pointed out.

13:451:25520:28:18:89:539:215:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The tax on wealth does not fall towards zero, indeed, the opposite is true. As we
13:452:25601:18:18:72:540:197:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:illustrate below the tax can be quite sizable and rise over time. The solution does not
13:453:25688:18:18:72:540:179:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:converge to an interior allocation and multipliers do not converge, invalidating the appli-
13:454:25779:18:18:72:374:161:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:cationJudd(1985), as we summarized here in Theorem1.
13:455:25831:18:18:89:539:143:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Perhaps counterintuitively, the long-run tax on capital is inversely related to the level
13:456:25920:18:18:72:540:125:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:of government spending. The reason for this is that the solution drives capital to its lowest
13:457:26013:18:17:72:540:107:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:feasible valuekg, which is increasing in spendingg. Thus, a lower level of spending
13:458:26096:17:18:72:540:90:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:allows the planner to take long run capital to a lower level. This emphasizes that positive
13:459:26187:18:0:72:454:72:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:long-run taxation of wealth is not being driven by a budgetary necessity.

15:515:28624:18:18:89:539:397:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:A few things stand out in Figure1. First, the results confirm what we showed theoret-

15:521:29096:18:18:89:540:290:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Second, forσ<1, the path for capital is not monotonic13and eventually converges to

15:524:29356:18:18:72:540:236:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:for any periodt, the solution should converge to that of the logarithmic utility case as
15:525:29444:18:18:72:540:218:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:B:σ→1.14By implication, forσ<1 the rate of convergence to the zero-tax steady state
15:526:29525:18:18:72:540:200:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:must be zero asσ↑1. To further punctuate this point, Figure2shows the number of

15:528:29692:18:18:72:375:164:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:it takes longer and longer and asσ↑1 it takes an eternity.
15:529:29750:18:19:89:540:146:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The logarithmic case leaves other imprints on the solutions forσ�=1. Returning to
15:530:29831:19:12:81:519:127:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:12This depends on the level of initial capital. For lower levels of capital the path first rises then falls.
15:531:29939:12:16:81:540:115:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:13This is possible because the state variable has two dimensions,(kt,Ct−1). At the optimum, for the same

16:540:30337:14:15:72:540:534:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:solid line uses the solution of the nonlinear model, the dashed line uses an approximation

16:542:30459:31:18:72:540:488:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Figure1, for bothσ<1 andσ>1 we see that over the first 20-30 years, the path ap-
16:543:30539:18:18:72:540:470:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:proaches the steady state of the logarithmic utility case, associated with a tax rate around

16:545:30710:17:18:72:540:435:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:explained by the fact that forσ=1 it is driven by the standard rate of convergence in the
16:546:30799:18:18:72:540:417:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:neoclassical growth model. The solution path then transitions much more slowly either
16:547:30884:18:36:72:409:399:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:upwards or downwards, depending on whetherσ<1 orσ>1.
16:548:30936:36:18:72:540:363:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:An Intuition based on the Intertemporal Manipulation of Saving Incentives.Why
16:549:31013:18:18:72:540:345:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:does the tax rise forσ>1 and fall forσ<1? Why are these dynamics relatively slow for
16:550:31097:18:18:72:120:327:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:B:σnear 1?
16:551:31105:18:18:89:539:309:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:To address these questions about normative results, it helps to back up and review
16:552:31187:18:18:72:540:291:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:differences in the following positive exercise. Start from a constant tax on wealth and
16:553:31274:18:18:72:540:273:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:imagine an unexpected announcement for higher future taxation. How do capitalists re-
16:554:31359:18:18:72:540:255:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:act today? There are substitution and income effects pulling in opposite directions. When
16:555:31448:18:18:72:539:237:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:B:σ>1 the substitution effect is weaker and capitalists increase present savings, to partially
16:556:31540:18:17:72:540:219:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:offset the drop in future consumption.15Whenσ<1 the substitution effect is stronger
16:557:31623:17:18:72:540:202:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and capitalists decrease present savings, substituting towards current consumption. In
16:558:31709:18:18:72:539:184:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the logarithmic case,σ=1, the two effects cancel out, so that present consumption and
16:559:31794:18:18:72:193:166:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:savings are unaffected.
16:560:31817:18:18:89:539:148:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Returning to the normative questions, increasing savings is desirable when capital is
16:561:31902:18:19:72:540:130:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:currently being taxed, so as to augment the tax base. Whenσ<1, this can be accom-
16:562:31983:19:16:81:539:111:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:15This does not imply that the supply for savings “bends backward”. For instance, if the interest rate
16:563:32085:16:12:72:540:95:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:were lowered permanently then wealth would rises over time, even withσ>1. Higher values ofσare
16:564:32179:12:11:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:simply associated with a less elastic savings response. Although there is no consensus, the case withσ>1
16:565:32283:11:0:72:297:72:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:is usually considered the empirically plausible one.
17:566:32337:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:plished by promising lower tax rates in the future; the optimum leans in this direction
17:567:32424:18:18:72:539:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:explaining the declining path for taxes. In contrast, whenσ>1, the same is accom-
17:568:32505:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:plished by promising higher future tax rates; this leads to an increasing path for taxes.
17:569:32594:18:18:72:539:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:These incentives are absent in the logarithmic,σ=1, case, explaining why the tax rate
17:570:32679:18:18:72:198:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:converges to a constant.
17:571:32703:18:18:89:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Whenσ<1, the rate of convergence to the zero-tax steady state is driven by these
17:572:32783:18:18:72:539:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:considerations to manipulate savings intertemporally. Withσnear 1, the potency and
17:573:32865:18:36:72:525:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:benefit of these manipulations is small, explaining why the rate of convergence is low.
17:574:32952:36:18:72:539:546:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Positive weight on capitalistsγ>0.At least withg=0, a desire for redistribution is
17:575:33034:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:crucial to make the question of wealth taxing nontrivial. Proposition3assumes no weight
17:576:33121:18:18:72:530:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:on capitalists,γ=0, ensuring that redistribution is desired from capitalists to workers.
17:577:33209:18:18:89:539:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:When the desire for redistribution is present but weak, so thatγis positive but low,
17:578:33293:18:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:it is natural to expect the same qualitatively results as Proposition3. Whenγis very
17:579:33377:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:high, however, desired redistribution may flip and run from workers to capitalists. It is
17:580:33466:18:18:72:539:438:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:then natural to expect subsidies on wealth, rather than taxes. Figure3verifies all of these
17:581:33557:18:36:72:338:420:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:points, fixingσ=1.25 and varying the weightγ.16
17:582:33604:36:18:72:540:384:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Nonlinear and Linearized Dynamics.The policy functions associated with the Bellman
17:583:33686:18:18:72:535:366:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:equation (4) map(kt,Ct−1)into(kt+1,Ct). It is useful to consider the resulting dynamics.
17:584:33774:18:18:89:539:348:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Numerically, whenσ<1 we find that the zero-tax steady state is globally stable:
17:585:33853:18:17:72:540:330:155:g_d0_f7:143:g_d0_f3:B:(kt,Ct−1)converges from any initial condition, even those not satisfying the initial con-
17:586:33942:17:18:72:539:313:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ditionVC=0. Whenσ>1 there are three relevant steady states: two corners, atkgand
17:587:34022:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:kg, and the zero-tax interior steady state. We find that the latter is saddle path stable. We

18:645:35901:28:28:72:319:270:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 4.Consider the linearized system(5),
18:646:35949:28:28:82:365:242:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(a)Ifσ>1, the zero-tax steady state is saddle-path stable.
18:647:36007:28:28:81:368:214:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(b)Ifσ<1andγ≤γ∗, the zero-tax steady state is stable.
18:648:36060:28:18:82:540:186:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(c)Ifσ<1andγ>γ∗, the zero-tax steady state may be stable or unstable and the dynamics
18:649:36145:18:27:101:192:168:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:may feature cycles.
18:650:36164:27:18:89:539:141:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:Here,γ∗=u�(c∗)/U�(C∗)is the weight on capitalists which makes the planner indifferent
18:651:36249:18:28:72:462:123:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:between redistributing towards workers or capitalists at the zero-tax steady state.
18:652:36332:28:18:72:540:95:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:The first two points confirm our theoretical and numerical observations for the nonlinear
18:653:36421:18:0:72:539:77:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:dynamical system. Forσ<1 the zero tax steady state is locally stable, while forσ>1 it is
19:654:36511:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:locally saddle-path stable, which explains why the solution does not generally converge
19:655:36598:18:18:72:288:690:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:to this steady state, as discussed above.17
19:656:36641:18:18:89:539:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The third point shows that for highγthe system may become unstable or feature
19:657:36718:18:18:72:539:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:cyclical dynamics. This is consistent withKemp et al.(1993), which studied the linear
19:658:36803:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics around the zero-tax steady state and reported the potential for instability and
19:659:36891:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:cycles. Our proposition clarifies that a necessary condition for their results is an assumed
19:660:36983:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:desire to redistribute away from workers towards capitalists,γ>γ∗. Instead, when
19:661:37063:18:18:72:539:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:desired redistribution runs from capitalists to workers, so thatγ<γ∗(or whenσ>1 for
19:662:37146:18:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:anyγ) the linearized dynamics cannot feature cycles. Our paper focuses on low values of
19:663:37233:18:18:72:539:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:B:γ, to ensure redistribution from capitalists to workers. Thus, our results are completely
19:664:37322:18:40:72:281:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:unrelated to those inKemp et al.(1993).
19:665:37361:40:27:72:341:488:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:2.3  Ad Hoc Saving Rules for Capitalists
19:666:37401:27:17:72:540:461:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Up to this point, in keeping withJudd(1985), capitalists have been modeled as infinitely-
19:667:37490:17:18:72:540:444:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:lived optimizing savers. In addition, we specialized to additively separable utility func-
19:668:37580:18:18:72:370:426:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tions. We now relax both assumptions in one fell swoop.
19:669:37635:18:33:89:420:408:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Assume capitalists save according to an “ad-hoc” savings rule,
19:670:37697:33:33:226:385:375:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:A:kt+1=S(Rtkt;Rt+1,Rt+2,...),
19:671:37724:33:18:72:539:342:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:whereS(I;R1,R2,...)is some given savings function, taking as arguments current wealth
19:672:37809:18:18:72:540:324:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:I=Rtktand all future interest rates{Rt+1,Rt+2,...}. This encompasses the case where
19:673:37892:18:18:72:540:306:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:capitalists maximize an additively separable utility function, but is more general. For ex-
19:674:37983:18:18:72:540:288:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ample, the savings function may be derived from the maximization of a recursive utility
19:675:38070:18:17:72:540:270:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:function, or even represent behavior that cannot be captured by optimization, such as hy-
19:676:38159:17:18:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:perbolic discounting or self-control and temptation. This generality will help us discern
19:677:38248:18:18:72:442:235:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the key economic mechanism involved in our non-convergence result.
19:678:38314:18:38:89:219:217:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The planning problem is
19:679:38337:38:9:231:254:179:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:max

19:683:38354:11:0:267:282:166:80:g_d0_f5:80:g_d0_f3:F:t=0
19:684:38357:0:30:285:392:179:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:A:βt(u(ct)+γU(Ct)),
19:685:38374:30:15:81:539:149:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:17One can employ the linear system to compute the number of years before the tax rate falls below 1%,
19:686:38475:15:12:72:540:134:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:a calculation comparable to that performed earlier for the nonlinear model. The dotted line in Figure2
19:687:38577:12:12:72:540:122:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:displays the result, which comes out very close to the nonlinear model. By this measure, forσ<1, the
19:688:38677:12:0:72:370:110:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:dynamics appear to be well approximated by the linearized system.
20:689:38744:0:33:72:122:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:subject to

20:694:38828:36:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Non Convergence.Our next result provides a generalization of the negative conclusion
20:695:38912:18:28:72:354:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:in Proposition2to our current ad hoc savings setting.
20:696:38965:28:18:72:539:518:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 5.Supposeγ=0and assume the savings function is increasing in income, so that
20:697:39053:18:18:72:540:500:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:SI(I,R1,R2,...)≥0, and decreasing in future rates, so that SRτ(I,R1,R2,...)≤0for all
20:698:39137:18:28:72:447:482:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f5:C:τ=1, 2, . . .Then the optimum does not converge to the zero-tax steady state.
20:699:39214:28:17:89:540:454:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:The requirement that savings increase with wealth,SI≥0, amounts to a standard
20:700:39291:17:18:72:540:437:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:normality condition. When in addition higher future interest rates lower current sav-
20:701:39376:18:18:72:540:419:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ings,SRτ≤0, the economy cannot converge to the zero-tax steady state. The case with
20:702:39459:18:18:72:497:401:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:separable isoelastic utility withσ>1 is a special case satisfying these properties.
20:703:39542:18:18:89:539:383:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:As before, the intuition is that the anticipatory effects create the potential to manip-
20:704:39630:18:18:72:540:365:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ulate savings. The planner makes use of these incentives, creating a destabilizing force
20:705:39718:18:36:72:204:347:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:away from zero taxation.
20:706:39742:36:18:72:539:311:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Elasticities and Taxation.Propositions2and5show that an interior steady state is not
20:707:39826:18:18:72:540:293:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:something one can take for granted. Casting these important warnings aside, let us now
20:708:39912:18:18:72:520:275:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:proceed assuming we do reach an interior steady state for quantities and multipliers.

21:753:41559:28:17:89:539:412:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:With additive separable utility, the long run elasticity of savings is often characterized

22:780:43889:47:27:72:540:553:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:3  Representative Agent Ramsey Model: Chamley (1986)
22:781:43941:27:31:97:298:526:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:and Judd (1999) Revisited
22:782:43966:31:18:72:539:495:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Up to this point we worked within the two-class model introduced byJudd(1985), with-
22:783:44050:18:18:72:540:477:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:out government debt.Chamley(1986) worked with a representative agent Ramsey model
22:784:44131:18:18:72:540:459:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:with unconstrained government debt.Judd(1999) adopts the same assumptions. This
22:785:44210:18:18:72:540:441:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:section presents results using a representative agent model, directly comparable to these
22:786:44299:18:18:72:134:423:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:two papers.
22:787:44310:18:17:89:539:405:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We first discuss the solution when the bounds on capital taxation do not bind in the
22:788:44394:17:41:72:452:388:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:long run. We then discuss the possibility of bounds binding indefinitely.
22:789:44467:41:26:72:383:347:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:3.1  First Best or Zero Taxation of Zero Wealth?
22:790:44515:26:18:72:540:321:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Just asJudd(1985),Chamley(1986) considered non-additively separable utility to avoid
22:791:44599:18:18:72:540:303:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:an “infinite long-run elasticity of savings”, as the additively separable utility case is com-
22:792:44693:18:18:72:539:285:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:monly characterized.20Unlike additively separable utility, recursive preferences allows
22:793:44780:18:18:72:540:267:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the rate of impatience to vary with consumption levels. We will show that, if the optimum
22:794:44869:18:18:72:540:249:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:converges to a steady state where bounds on taxation are not binding, then the tax on cap-
22:795:44959:18:18:72:540:231:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ital is indeed zero. However, the model yields other, hitherto unnoticed, implications as
22:796:45048:18:18:72:310:213:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:long as the rate of impatience is not constant.
22:797:45095:18:18:89:539:195:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:To distinguish this subsection from the next, we focus here on situations where the
22:798:45178:18:18:72:540:177:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:bounds on capital taxation are not binding in the long run. The next subsection addresses
22:799:45267:18:19:72:370:159:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the important possibility of indefinitely binding bounds.
22:800:45324:19:16:81:539:140:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:19The derivation also assumes there are no bounds on capital taxation. As we shall see, this is crucial in
22:801:45430:16:8:72:252:124:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:the context of theChamley(1986) model.
22:802:45468:8:16:81:539:116:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:20At any steady state with additive utility one must haveR=1/βfor a fixed parameterβ∈(0, 1). This
22:803:45565:16:12:72:540:100:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:is true regardless of the wealth or consumption level. In this sense, the supply of savings is infinitely elastic
22:804:45678:12:0:72:167:88:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:at this rate of interest.

25:880:49875:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:unconstrained so that the solution approaches a steady state where the bounds do not
25:881:49959:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:bind, there are two possibilities. In the first, the tax base for capital taxation must have
25:882:50051:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:been driven to zero, perhaps due to its heavy taxation in the transition to the steady
25:883:50137:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:state. The second possibility is that the government accumulate enough wealth against
25:884:50222:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the private sector, perhaps aided by heavy taxation of capital, to finance itself without the
25:885:50315:18:18:72:315:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:distortionary taxation, achieving the first best.
25:886:50364:18:18:89:539:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Both scenarios require the government to accumulate a significant positive assets po-
25:887:50449:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:sition, i.e. negative debt. In the first case, sinceat=kt+bt→0, the government must
25:888:50532:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:own the entire capital stock. In the second, the government must accumulate enough as-
25:889:50618:17:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:sets to finance government spending, forgoing labor and capital taxation. Quantitatively,
25:890:50707:18:18:72:491:439:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the second scenario is likely to require greater asset accumulation than the first.
25:891:50790:18:18:89:539:421:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Both these scenarios are markedly different from the usual interpretation of the zero
25:892:50875:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:long-run tax result, which implies that we should forego obtaining revenue from capital
25:893:50962:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:taxation but not from labor taxation—relatively unfriendly to capital taxation. Instead,
25:894:51050:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:here both labor and capital are either treated symmetrically or nothing remains to be
25:895:51135:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:taxed in the case of capital—a scenario that is downright friendly to capital taxation, more
25:896:51227:18:18:72:197:331:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:symmetrical with labor.
25:897:51250:18:18:89:539:313:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:To be sure, in the special, but commonly assumed, case with additive separable utility,
25:898:51337:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:positive private wealth, a zero tax on wealth and a positive tax on labor coexist at a steady
25:899:51430:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:state. However, this is not possible whenever the rate of impatience is locally not constant.
25:900:51523:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:In this sense, the usual interpretation—where labor bears the entire burden of taxation
25:901:51610:18:40:72:338:241:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and private wealth is spared—is a knife edge case.
25:902:51660:40:26:72:373:201:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:3.2  Long Run Capital Taxes with Constraints
25:903:51704:26:18:72:540:175:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:As is well understood, without constraints on capital taxation the problem of capital tax-
25:904:51794:18:18:72:540:157:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ation becomes trivial: the solution involves extraordinarily high initial capital taxation,
25:905:51885:18:18:72:540:139:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:typically complete expropriation, unless the first best is achieved first. Taxing the given
25:906:51976:18:18:72:540:121:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:initial capital stock mimics the missing lump-sum tax, which has no distortionary effects.
25:907:52066:18:0:89:539:103:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:This motivatedChamley(1986) and the subsequent literature to impose upper bounds
26:908:52148:0:18:72:539:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:on taxation,τt≤ ̄τ.24We now show that these bounds on capital taxes may bind forever,
26:909:52233:18:18:72:539:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:contradicting a claim byChamley(1986). This claim has been echoed throughout the
26:910:52313:18:18:72:384:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:literature, e.g.Judd(1999),Atkeson et al.(1999) and others.
26:911:52372:18:18:89:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:For our present purposes, and followingChamley(1986), as well asJudd(1999), it is
26:912:52453:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:convenient to work with a continuous-time version of the model and restrict attention to
26:913:52541:18:20:72:254:618:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:additively separable preferences,25
26:914:52576:20:27:257:277:598:143:g_d0_f12:80:g_d0_f6:C:ˆ∞

26:927:52907:18:33:72:249:454:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:crucial. The resource constraint is

26:933:53114:28:18:72:540:324:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:wherea0=k0+b0denotes initial private wealth, consisting of capitalk0and bondsb0.
26:934:53194:18:33:72:370:306:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:To enforce bounds on capital taxation we further impose
26:935:53249:33:18:259:540:273:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:A:θt=uc(ct,nt),(14a)

26:940:53337:21:16:81:539:168:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:24A typical story for the bounds is tax compliance constraints—capital owners would hide capital or
26:941:53436:16:12:72:540:152:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:mask its returns if taxation were too onerous. Another motivation, although outside the present scope of

26:943:53641:11:12:72:539:129:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:capital owners, a point made bySaez(2013). Finally, another possibility is that bounds on capital taxation
26:944:53747:12:9:72:509:117:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:reflect self-imposed institutional constraints introduced to mitigate the time inconsistency problem.
26:945:53848:9:16:81:540:108:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:25Continuous time allowedChamley(1986) to exploit the bang-bang nature of the optimal solution. Since
26:946:53949:16:12:72:540:92:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:we focus on cases where this is not the case it is less crucial for our results. However, we prefer to keep the
26:947:54060:12:0:72:166:80:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:analyses comparable.
27:948:54082:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:for some bound ̄τ>0.  The planning problem maximizes (11a) subject to (12), (13)
27:949:54162:18:18:72:118:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and (14).
27:950:54171:18:18:89:539:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Chamley(1986, Theorem 2, pg. 615) formulated the following claim regarding the
27:951:54249:18:28:72:254:654:143:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic path of capital taxation.26
27:952:54284:28:18:72:540:626:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Claim.Suppose ̄τ=1and that preferences are given by(11). Then there exists a time T with the

27:954:54403:28:28:82:309:580:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(a)for t<T, the constraintτt≤ ̄τis binding;
27:955:54446:28:28:81:372:552:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(b)for t>T capital income is untaxed: rt=r∗tandτt=0;
27:956:54498:28:28:82:139:524:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:(c)T<∞.
27:957:54505:28:18:89:540:496:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:At a crucial juncture in the proof of this claim,Chamley(1986) states in support of part
27:958:54593:18:17:72:540:478:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(c) that “The constraintrt≥0 cannot be binding forever (the marginal utility of private
27:959:54680:17:18:72:539:461:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:consumption [...] would grow to infinity [...] which is absurd).”27Our next proposition
27:960:54767:18:18:72:540:443:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:establishes that there is nothing absurd about this within the logic of the model and that,
27:961:54858:18:18:72:540:425:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:quite to the contrary, part (c) of the above claim is incorrect: indefinite taxation,T=∞,
27:962:54947:18:28:72:158:407:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:may be optimal.
27:963:54962:28:18:72:539:379:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 8.Suppose ̄τ=1and that preferences are given by(11)withσ>1. Fix any initial
27:964:55049:18:18:72:540:361:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:capital stock k0. There exists b< ̄b such that for b0∈[b, ̄b]the optimum hasτt= ̄τfor all t≥0,
27:965:55143:18:28:72:489:343:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:i.e. the bound on capital taxation binds forever, and there is no equilibrium with b> ̄b.
27:966:55232:28:18:89:539:315:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Here ̄brepresents the peak of a “Laffer curve”, above which there is no equilibrium.
27:967:55316:18:18:72:540:297:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:The proposition states that for intermediate debt levels it is optimal to tax capital indefi-
27:968:55409:18:18:72:540:279:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:nitely. Since these points are below the peak of the Laffer curve, indefinite taxation is not
27:969:55502:18:18:72:539:261:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:driven by budgetary need—there are feasible plans withT<∞, however, the plan with
27:970:55583:18:18:72:539:243:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:T=∞is simply better. This is illustrated in figure4with a qualitative plot of the set of
27:971:55671:18:17:72:540:225:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:states(k0,b0)for which indefinite capital taxation is optimal. Although this proposition
27:972:55759:17:18:72:539:208:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:only considers ̄τ=1, as inChamley(1986), it is natural to conjecture that lower values of
27:973:55848:18:18:73:304:190:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B: ̄τmake the optimality ofT=∞more likely.
27:974:55888:18:18:89:539:172:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Our next result assumesg=0 and constructs the solution for a set of initial conditions
27:975:55974:18:20:72:291:154:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that allow us to guess and verify its form.
27:976:56017:20:12:81:461:134:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:26Similar claims are made inAtkeson et al.(1999),Judd(1999) and many other papers.
27:977:56099:12:16:81:539:122:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:27It is worth pointing out, however that althoughChamley(1986) claimsT<∞it never states thatTis
27:978:56194:16:12:72:540:106:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:small. Indeed, it cautions to the possibility that it is quite large saying “the length of the period with capital
27:979:56308:12:0:72:330:94:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:income taxation at the 100 per cent rate can be significant.”
28:980:56371:0:45:299:333:659:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f6:C:T=∞
28:981:56374:45:30:299:333:614:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f6:C:T<∞

28:985:56432:35:18:72:540:518:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 9.Suppose that ̄τ=1, that preferences are given by(11)withσ>1, and that

28:987:56604:18:18:72:540:482:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:optimum satisfiesτt= ̄τfor all t≥0and ct,kt,nt→0exponentially with constant nt/ktand

28:989:56694:28:18:89:539:436:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:This proposition shows that for well chosen initial conditions and no government
28:990:56774:18:18:72:540:418:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:spending, the solution path converges to zero in an homogenous, constant growth rate
28:991:56858:18:17:72:540:400:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:fashion. This feature is certainly special, yet helpful in constructing the appropriate guess
28:992:56951:17:18:72:123:383:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:explicitly.
28:993:56962:18:18:89:539:365:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:This explicit example illustrates that convergence takes place, but not to an interior
28:994:57048:18:18:72:540:347:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:steady state. Indeed, with additive separable utility no interior steady state exists when
28:995:57138:18:18:72:539:329:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:T=∞. With ̄τ=1 the after tax interest rate is zero when the bound is binding, but
28:996:57219:18:18:72:540:311:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the agent discounts the future positively, preventing a steady state. Instead, with ̄τ<1
28:997:57307:18:18:72:540:293:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the interest rate may be positive and the after tax interest could equal the discount rateρ.
28:998:57399:18:18:72:540:275:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:With additive separable utility, this ensures constant consumption, but does not ensure
28:999:57486:18:18:72:540:257:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:constant labor. If the tax on labor is not constant then labor is generally not constant.
28:1000:57575:18:18:72:540:239:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Indeed, this appears to be a feature of the optimum, with the planner neutralizing the
28:1001:57661:18:18:72:540:221:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:intertemporal substitution of labor, induced by the capital tax, with an ever increasing
28:1002:57749:18:18:72:539:203:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:labor tax. We conjecture that a steady state withT=∞may be possible if the tax on\
28:1003:57831:18:40:72:308:185:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:labor is also constrained by an upper bound.
28:1004:57875:40:26:72:249:145:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:3.3  Revisiting Judd (1999)
28:1005:57902:26:18:72:540:119:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Up to this point we have focused on the Chamley-Judd zero-tax results. A followup
28:1006:57983:18:18:72:540:101:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:literature has offered both extensions and interpretations. One notable case doing both
28:1007:58070:18:0:72:540:83:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:isJudd(1999). This paper followsChamley(1986) closely, setting up a representative
29:1008:58154:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:agent economy with perfect financial markets and unrestricted government bonds. More
29:1009:58238:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:specifically, the paper does two things. First, it provides a variant of the result inChamley
29:1010:58331:18:18:72:539:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(1986) which does not require the allocation nor multipliers to converge to a steady state.
29:1011:58422:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Instead, the paper postulates that an endogenous multiplier lies within an interval and
29:1012:58509:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:shows that this implies that capital taxation must be zero on average. Second, the paper
29:1013:58597:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:offers a connection between capital taxation and rising consumption taxes to provides
29:1014:58682:18:36:72:392:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:intuition for these results. Let us consider each point in turn.
29:1015:58746:36:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Bounded Multipliers and Zero Average Capital Taxes.Using our setup from Section
29:1016:58825:18:18:72:539:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:3.2the main result can be restated as follows. Assuming ̄τ=1, then the planning problem
29:1017:58912:18:18:72:539:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:maximizes (11a) subject to (12), (13), (14a), (14b), andrt≥0. LetˆΛt=e−ρtθtΛtdenote the
29:1018:58999:18:19:72:539:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:co-state for capital, i.e. the multiplier on equation (12), satisfying ̇ˆΛt=ρˆΛt−r∗tˆΛt. Using

30:1091:61742:36:18:72:540:243:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Exploding Consumption Taxes.Judd(1999) also offers an intuitive interpretation for
30:1092:61824:18:18:72:540:225:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the Chamley-Judd result pointing out that a tax on capital is equivalent to an increasing
30:1093:61913:18:18:72:540:207:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tax on consumption. This casts indefinite taxation of capital as a villain, since increasing
30:1094:62005:18:18:72:540:189:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and unbounded taxes on consumption do not seem intuitively reasonable and seemingly
30:1095:62088:18:18:72:539:171:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:contradict standard commodity tax principles, as enunciated byDiamond and Mirrlees

30:1097:62216:18:18:89:539:135:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We believe the equivalence between capital taxation and a rising path for consump-
30:1098:62298:18:18:72:540:117:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tion taxes is accurate and useful. It does explain why prolonging capital taxation comes
30:1099:62386:18:16:81:539:99:57:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:29In this continuous time optimal control formulation, the costate equation for capital is the counterpart
30:1100:62492:16:11:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:to the first-order condition with respect to capital in a discrete time formulation. Indeed, the same result
30:1101:62600:11:0:72:292:72:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:can be easily formulated in a discrete time setting.
31:1102:62654:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:at an efficiency cost by distorting the consumption path. If the marginal cost from this
31:1103:62742:18:18:72:539:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:distortion were increasing inTand approached infinity atT=∞this would indeed im-
31:1104:62822:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ply insurmountable costs and provide a strong argument against indefinite taxation of
31:1105:62907:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:capital. An instinctive aversion to consumption taxes that rise without bound is perhaps
31:1106:62995:18:18:72:284:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:based on an intuition for this possibility.
31:1107:63038:18:18:89:539:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We next formalize the efficiency costs of capital taxation generated by the intertempo-
31:1108:63125:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ral distortions to the consumption path. However, despite the connection with ever in-
31:1109:63211:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:creasing consumption taxes, we show that the marginal cost of these distortions remains
31:1110:63298:18:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:bounded, even asT→∞, so that there are no insurmountable costs. These bounded
31:1111:63375:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:marginal costs must be traded off against the marginal benefits, explaining why the cor-
31:1112:63463:18:18:72:539:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ner solutionT=∞is potentially optimal. The intuitive argument against capital taxation
31:1113:63549:18:18:72:492:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:based on a connection with ever increasing consumption taxes does not deliver.
31:1114:63627:18:18:89:539:492:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We proceed with a constructive argument and assume, for simplicity, that technology
31:1115:63710:18:23:72:451:474:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:is linear, so thatf(k,n)−δk=r∗k+w∗nfor fixed parametersr∗andn∗.

31:1136:64392:18:18:72:540:161:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the scenes, the static problem solves the dynamic problem. In particular, it optimizes over
31:1137:64483:18:18:72:540:143:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the path for labor taxes. In this static representation, 1+ψ(T)is akin to a production cost
31:1138:64574:18:18:72:539:125:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f5:B:of consumption andτ(T)to a non-distortionary capital levy. On the one hand, higherT
31:1139:64657:18:18:72:540:107:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:increases the efficiency cost from the consumption path. On the other hand, it increases
31:1140:64745:18:17:72:540:89:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:revenue in proportion to the level of initial capital. Prolonging capital taxation requires
31:1141:64836:17:0:72:258:72:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:trading off these costs and benefits.
32:1142:64875:0:18:89:539:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Importantly, despite the connection between capital taxation and an ever increasing,
32:1143:64959:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:unbounded tax on consumption, the proposition shows that the tradeoff between costs
32:1144:65042:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and benefits is bounded,dψdτ<∞, even asT→∞. In other words, indefinite taxation
32:1145:65121:18:18:72:526:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:does not come at an infinite marginal cost and helps explain why this may be optimal.
32:1146:65206:18:18:89:539:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Should we be surprised that these results contradict commodity tax principles, as
32:1147:65287:18:18:72:539:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:enunciated byDiamond and Mirrlees(1971),Atkinson and Stiglitz(1972) and others? No,
32:1148:65370:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:not at all. As general as these frameworks may be they do not consider upper bounds on
32:1149:65456:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:taxation, the crucial ingredient inChamley(1986) andJudd(1999). Thus, their guiding
32:1150:65539:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:principles are ill adapted to these settings. In particular, formulas based on local elas-
32:1151:65629:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:ticities do not apply, without further modification. When bounds are introduced, this
32:1152:65714:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:constrains taxation to be lower in the short run, but spreads it over a longer, possibly
32:1153:65802:18:46:72:160:510:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:infinite, horizon.
32:1154:65820:46:31:72:376:464:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:4  A Hybrid: Redistribution and Debt
32:1155:65856:31:18:72:540:433:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:Throughout this paper we have strived to stay on target and remain faithful to the original
32:1156:65947:18:18:72:540:415:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:models supporting the Chamley-Judd result. This is important so that our own results are
32:1157:66035:18:18:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:easily comparable to those inJudd(1985) andChamley(1986). However, many contribu-
32:1158:66116:18:18:72:540:379:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tions since then offer modifications and extensions of the original Chamley-Judd models
32:1159:66203:18:18:72:540:361:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and results. In this section we depart briefly from our main focus to show that our results
32:1160:66294:18:18:72:482:343:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:transcend their original boundaries and are relevant to this broader literature.
32:1161:66374:18:18:89:539:325:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:To make this point with a relevant example, we consider a hybrid model, with redistri-
32:1162:66460:18:18:72:539:307:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:bution between capitalists and workers as inJudd(1985), but sharing the essential feature
32:1163:66549:18:18:72:540:289:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:inChamley(1986) of unrestricted government debt. It is very simple to modify the model
32:1164:66635:18:18:72:540:271:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:in Section2in this way. We add bonds to the wealth of capitalistsat=kt+bt, modifying
32:1165:66719:18:18:72:153:253:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:equation (1c) to
32:1166:66735:18:25:184:427:235:143:g_d0_f4:155:g_d0_f7:C:βU�(Ct)(Ct+kt+1+bt+1)=U�(Ct−1)(kt+bt)
32:1167:66772:25:18:72:539:210:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and the transversality condition toβtU�(Ct)(kt+1+bt+1)→0. Equivalently, we have the
32:1168:66855:18:25:72:279:192:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:present valueimplementability condition,
32:1169:66895:25:15:214:222:167:80:g_d0_f6:80:g_d0_f6:F:∞
32:1170:66896:15:11:212:225:152:280:g_d0_f6:280:g_d0_f6:C:∑
32:1171:66897:11:0:211:225:141:80:g_d0_f5:80:g_d0_f3:F:t=0
32:1172:66900:0:0:228:401:154:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:A:βtU�(Ct)Ct=U�(C0)R0(k0+b0),
33:1173:66929:0:38:72:251:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:WithU(C)=C1−σ/(1−σ)this is
33:1174:66955:38:0:198:236:670:155:g_d0_f7:155:g_d0_f7:C:(1−σ)
33:1175:66960:0:15:242:250:683:80:g_d0_f6:80:g_d0_f6:F:∞
33:1176:66961:15:10:239:252:668:280:g_d0_f6:280:g_d0_f6:C:∑
33:1177:66962:10:0:238:253:658:80:g_d0_f5:80:g_d0_f3:F:t=0
33:1178:66965:0:42:255:540:670:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:A:βtU(Ct)=U�(C0)R0(k0+b0).(16)
33:1179:66993:42:18:72:539:628:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Anticipated Confiscatory Taxation.Forσ>1 the left hand side in equation (16) is
33:1180:67072:18:17:72:539:610:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:decreasing inCtand the right hand side is decreasing inC0. It follows that one can take a
33:1181:67161:17:18:72:540:593:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:limit with the property thatCt→0 for allt=0, 1, . . . , which is optimal forγ=0. Along
33:1182:67247:18:18:72:539:575:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:this limitR1→0, so the tax on capital is exploding to infinity. This same logic applies if
33:1183:67337:18:18:72:540:557:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:the tax is temporarily restricted for periodst≤T−1 for some givenT, but is unrestricted
33:1184:67424:18:28:72:134:539:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:in periodT.
33:1185:67435:28:18:72:540:511:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 11.Consider the two-class model from Section2but with unrestricted government
33:1186:67524:18:18:72:539:493:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:bonds. Supposeσ>1andγ=0. If capital taxation is unrestricted in at least one period, then
33:1187:67613:18:28:72:469:475:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:the optimum features an infinite tax in some period and Ct→0for all t=0, 1, . . .
33:1188:67694:28:18:89:539:447:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:This result exemplifies how extreme the tax on capital may be without bounds. In
33:1189:67774:18:18:72:540:429:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:addition to this result and even whenσ<1, if no constraints are imposed on taxation,
33:1190:67858:18:18:72:539:411:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:except att=0, then in the continuous time limit as the length of time periods shrinks
33:1191:67943:18:18:72:540:393:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:to zero, taxation tends to infinity. This point was also raised inChamley(1986) for the
33:1192:68030:18:18:72:540:375:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:representative agent Ramsey model, and served as a motivation for imposing stationary
33:1193:68115:18:36:72:188:357:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:upper bounds,τt≤ ̄τ.
33:1194:68135:36:18:72:540:321:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f3:B:Long Run Taxation with Constraints.We now impose upper bounds on capital taxation
33:1195:68216:18:18:72:539:303:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and show that these constraints may bind forever, just as in Section3.2. As we did there,
33:1196:68305:18:27:72:430:285:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:it is convenient to switch to a continuous-time version of the model.
33:1197:68374:27:18:72:540:258:143:g_d0_f1:143:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 12.Consider the two-class model from Section2but with unrestricted government
33:1198:68463:18:18:72:539:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:bonds. Supposeσ>1andγ=0. If capital taxation is restricted byτt≤ ̄τfor some ̄τ>0, then
33:1199:68549:18:28:72:374:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:at the optimumτt= ̄τ, i.e. capital should be taxed indefinitely.
33:1200:68613:28:18:89:539:194:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:These results hold for any value of ̄τ>0, not just ̄τ=1. Intuitively,σ>1 is enough
33:1201:68695:18:18:72:539:176:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:to ensure indefinite taxation of capital becauseγ=0 makes it optimal to tax capitalists
33:1202:68782:18:18:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:as much as possible. Similar results hold for positive but low enough levels ofγ, so that
33:1203:68871:18:18:72:346:140:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:redistribution from capitalists to workers is desired.
33:1204:68925:18:18:89:539:122:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:This proposition assumes that transfers are perfectly targeted to workers. However,
33:1205:69008:18:18:72:539:104:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:indefinite taxation,T=∞, remains optimal when this assumption is relaxed, so that
33:1206:69089:18:0:72:284:86:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:transfers are also received by capitalists.
34:1207:69134:0:18:89:540:708:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We have also maintained the assumption fromJudd(1985) that workers do not save.
34:1208:69213:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:In a political economy context,Bassetto and Benhabib(2006) study a situation where all
34:1209:69299:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:agents save (in our context, both workers and capitalists) and are taxed linearly at the
34:1210:69387:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:same rate. Indeed, they report the possibility that indefinite taxation is optimal for the
34:1211:69477:18:18:72:145:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:median voter.
34:1212:69490:18:18:89:539:618:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, these results suggest that indefinite taxation is optimal in a range of models
34:1213:69577:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that are descendants of Chamley-Judd, with a wide range of assumptions regarding the
34:1214:69661:18:47:72:436:582:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:environment, heterogeneity, social objectives and policy instruments.
34:1215:69730:47:31:72:195:535:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:5  Conclusions
34:1216:69744:31:18:72:540:504:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:This study revisited two closely related models and results,Judd(1985) andChamley
34:1217:69825:18:17:72:539:486:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:(1986). Our own results contradict the standard results and their interpretation, revealing
34:1218:69916:17:18:72:442:469:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:that the long run tax on capital is not necessarily zero in these models.
34:1219:69989:18:18:89:539:451:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:Why were the proper conclusions missed byJudd(1985),Chamley(1986) and others?
34:1220:70066:18:18:72:540:433:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:These papers assume that endogenous multipliers associated with the planning problem
34:1221:70150:18:18:72:540:415:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:converge. We have shown that this is not necessarily the case. In fact, as we argued,
34:1222:70235:18:18:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:postulating convergence for endogenous multipliers is equivalent to postulating that the
34:1223:70323:18:18:72:540:379:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:planner’s marginal rate of substitution equals the planner’s, so that no intertemporal dis-
34:1224:70414:18:18:72:540:361:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:tortion is required. In this sense, assuming this convergence amounts to little more than
34:1225:70503:18:18:72:540:343:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:assuming zero long-run taxes. The original proofs are magically so simple that they al-
34:1226:70590:18:18:72:344:325:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:most feel too good to be true. And indeed, they are.
34:1227:70642:18:18:89:539:307:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:In quantitative evaluations it may well be the case that one finds a zero long-run tax
34:1228:70728:18:18:72:539:289:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:on capital, e.g. for the model inJudd(1985) one may setσ<1, and inChamley(1986) the
34:1229:70811:18:18:72:540:271:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:bounds may not bind forever, depending on parameters.30In this paper we stay away
34:1230:70892:18:18:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:from making any such claim, one way or another. We confined attention to the original
34:1231:70977:18:17:72:540:235:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:theoretical results, widely perceived as delivering zero long-run taxation as an ironclad
34:1232:71066:17:18:72:540:218:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:conclusion, independent of parameter values. Based on our analysis, we find little basis
34:1233:71154:18:47:72:210:200:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:for such an interpretation.
34:1234:71181:47:31:72:158:153:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:References

34:1237:71371:16:12:72:540:87:99:g_d0_f3:99:g_d0_f3:F:is optimal, the value ofTmay be high and it is possible that indefinite taxation provides a good approxi-

36:1289:74914:57:38:72:150:224:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:Appendix
36:1290:74922:38:28:72:275:186:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:A  Proof of Proposition3
36:1291:74946:28:14:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:The proof of Proposition3consists of three parts. In the first part, we provide a few
36:1292:75031:14:15:72:540:144:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:definitions that are necessary for the proof. In particular, we define thefeasibleset of
36:1293:75119:15:14:72:540:129:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:states. In the second part, we characterize the feasible set of states geometrically. The
36:1294:75208:14:15:72:540:115:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:proofs for the results are somewhat cumbersome and lengthy, so they are relegated to the
36:1295:75296:15:14:72:540:100:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:end of this section to ensure greater readability. Finally, in the third part, we use these
36:1296:75387:14:14:72:540:86:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:results to prove Proposition3. Readers interested only in the main steps of the proof are
36:1297:75476:14:0:72:291:72:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:advised to jump straight to the third part.
37:1298:75521:0:23:72:182:708:206:g_d0_f1:206:g_d0_f1:C:A.1  Definitions
37:1299:75537:23:15:72:540:685:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:For the proof of Proposition3we make a number of definitions, designed to simplify the
37:1300:75623:15:14:72:540:670:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:exposition. A state(k,C−)as in the recursive statement (4) of problem (1a) will sometimes

39:1455:80624:19:22:72:216:352:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.See subsectionA.4.2.

51:2142:105783:0:27:72:250:707:296:g_d0_f1:296:g_d0_f1:C:B  Numerical Method
51:2143:105802:27:15:72:539:680:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:To solve the Bellman equation we must first compute the setA. As is standard, in practice,
51:2144:105892:15:14:72:539:665:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:especially whenσ>1, we must restrict the range of capital to a closed interval[k, ̄k]with
51:2145:105981:14:15:72:540:651:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f3:B:k>0 to avoidk=0. This leads us to seek a subsetAk⊂A. We compute this set
51:2146:106053:15:17:72:195:636:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:numerically as follows.
51:2147:106076:17:0:89:293:619:143:g_d0_f3:155:g_d0_f7:A:Start with the setA0defined byC−=
51:2148:106109:0:11:298:315:626:80:g_d0_f3:80:g_d0_f4:F:1−β
51:2149:106112:11:0:304:385:615:80:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f3:A:βkandk∈[k,
51:2150:106122:0:22:387:539:623:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A: ̄k]. This set is self generating
51:2151:106155:22:14:72:539:601:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:and thusA0⊂Ak. We define an operator that finds all points(k,C−)for which one can
51:2152:106236:14:15:72:540:587:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:findc,K�,Csatisfying the constraints of the Bellman equation and(k�,C)∈A0. This gives
51:2153:106321:15:14:72:539:572:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:a setA1withA0⊂A1. Iterating on this procedure we obtainA0,A1,A2. . . and we stop
51:2154:106401:14:15:72:248:558:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:when the sets do not grow much.
51:2155:106432:15:14:89:539:543:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:A:We then solve the Bellman equation by value function iteration. We start with a guess
51:2156:106517:14:15:72:540:529:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:forV0that uses a feasible policy to evaluate utility. This ensures that our guess is be-
51:2157:106605:15:14:72:540:514:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:B:low the true value function. Iterating on the Bellman equation then leads to a monotone

53:2318:109545:26:25:101:528:386:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:C:In particular, there is a exactly one negative eigenvalue. The system is saddle-path stable.
